<div style="font-size: xx-small; line-height: 1.6em; margin-left: 60px;">This audio file was created from a revision of the article "<span class="fn">Kharkiv</span>" dated 2016-01-07, and does not reflect subsequent edits to the article. (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">Audio help</a>)</div>
<div style="text-align: center; clear: both"><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spoken_articles" title="Wikipedia:Spoken articles">More spoken articles</a></b></div>
</div>
<p><b>Kharkiv</b> (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Харків</span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Ukrainian" title="Help:IPA/Ukrainian">[ˈxɑrkiu̯]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-7">[6]</a></sup>, Russian: Харьков, Kharkov) is the second-largest city in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kharkiv:_.232_.2B_situation_October_2014_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kharkiv:_.232_.2B_situation_October_2014-8">[7]</a></sup> In the northeast of the country, it is the largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine" title="Sloboda Ukraine">Slobozhanshchyna</a> historical region. Kharkiv is the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_centre" title="Administrative centre">administrative centre</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Oblast" title="Kharkiv Oblast">Kharkiv Oblast</a> and of the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Raion" title="Kharkiv Raion">Kharkiv Raion</a>, though administratively it is incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/City_of_regional_significance_(Ukraine)" title="City of regional significance (Ukraine)">city of oblast significance</a> and does not belong to the raion. Population: <span class="nowrap">1, 439,036 (2017 est.)</span><sup id="cite_ref-ua2017estimate_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ua2017estimate-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was founded in 1654 and after a humble beginning as a small fortress grew to be a major centre of Ukrainian industry, trade and culture in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.</p>
<p>Kharkiv was the first capital of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, from December 1919 to January 1934, after which the capital relocated to <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-George_O._Liber_1992_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-George_O._Liber_1992-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Presently, Kharkiv is a major cultural, scientific, educational, transport and industrial centre of Ukraine, with 6 museums, 7 theatres and 80 libraries.</p>
<p>Its industry specializes primarily in <a href="/wiki/Machinery" class="mw-redirect" title="Machinery">machinery</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>. There are hundreds of industrial companies in the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Morozov_Design_Bureau" class="mw-redirect" title="Morozov Design Bureau">Morozov Design Bureau</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Malyshev_Tank_Factory" class="mw-redirect" title="Malyshev Tank Factory">Malyshev Tank Factory</a> (leaders in world <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tank</a> production from the 1930s to the 1980s); <a href="/wiki/Khartron" title="Khartron">Khartron</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear power plants</a> automation <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>); the <a href="/wiki/Turboatom" title="Turboatom">Turboatom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbines</a> for the hydro-, thermal- and nuclear-power plants), and <a href="/wiki/Antonov" title="Antonov">Antonov</a> (the multipurpose aircraft manufacturing plant).</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some sources indicate that the city may have been named after the Hunnic name for 'swan': <i>kharka</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Russian and Ukrainian Wikipedia cite more than 15 theories, and this one doesn't feature. The source is an advertising company. (May 2015)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other sources offer that the city was named after its near-legendary founder, <i>Kharko</i> (a <a href="/wiki/Diminutive" title="Diminutive">diminutive</a> form of the name <a href="/wiki/Chariton_(name)" title="Chariton (name)">Chariton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Харитон</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-KUW231114_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KUW231114-3">[2]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Zechariah_(given_name)" title="Zechariah (given name)">Zechariah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Захарій</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-wikisource_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikisource-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Kharkiv" title="Timeline of Kharkiv">Timeline of Kharkiv</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charkow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Charkow.jpg/150px-Charkow.jpg" width="150" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Charkow.jpg/225px-Charkow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Charkow.jpg/300px-Charkow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3171" data-file-height="2306" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charkow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
19th-century view of Kharkiv, with the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Cathedral,_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Assumption Cathedral, Kharkiv">Assumption Cathedral</a> belltower dominating the skyline.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sumskayaa_street,Kharkiv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg/150px-Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg/225px-Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg/300px-Sumskayaa_street%2CKharkiv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sumskayaa_street,Kharkiv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sumska_Street" title="Sumska Street">Sumska Street</a> is the main thoroughfare of Kharkiv</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cultural artifacts date back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, as well as those of later <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatian</a> settlers. There is also evidence that the <a href="/wiki/Chernyakhov_culture" title="Chernyakhov culture">Chernyakhov culture</a> flourished in the area from the second to the sixth centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment">Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city was founded by re-settlers who were running away from the war that engulfed <a href="/wiki/Right-bank_Ukraine" title="Right-bank Ukraine">Right-bank Ukraine</a> in 1654 (see <a href="/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising" title="Khmelnytsky Uprising">Khmelnytsky Uprising</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-KUW231114_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KUW231114-3">[2]</a></sup> The years before the region was a sparsely populated part of the <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Solchanyk2001_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solchanyk2001-13">[12]</a></sup> The group of people came onto the banks of <a href="/wiki/Lopan_River" title="Lopan River">Lopan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_River" title="Kharkiv River">Kharkiv</a> rivers where an abandoned settlement stood.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> According to archive documents, the leader of the re-settlers was <a href="/wiki/Otaman" class="mw-redirect" title="Otaman">otaman</a> Ivan Kryvoshlyk.<sup id="cite_ref-KUW231114_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KUW231114-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>At first the settlement was self-governed under the jurisdiction of a <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">voivode</a> from <a href="/wiki/Chuhuiv" title="Chuhuiv">Chuhuiv</a> that is 40 kilometres (25&#160;mi) to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The first appointed voivode from <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> was Voyin Selifontov in 1656 who started to build a local <a href="/wiki/Ostrog_(fortress)" title="Ostrog (fortress)">ostrog</a> (fort).<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> At that time the population of Kharkiv was just over 1000, half of whom were local cossacks, while Selifontov brought along a Moscow garrison of another 70 servicemen.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The first Kharkiv voivode was replaced in two years after constantly complaining that locals refused to cooperate in building the fort.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> Kharkiv also became the centre of the local Sloboda cossack regiment as the area surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Belgorod" title="Belgorod">Belgorod</a> fortress was being heavily militarized. With the resettlement of the area by Ukrainians it came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine" title="Sloboda Ukraine">Sloboda Ukraine</a>, most of which was included under the jurisdiction of the Razryad <a href="/wiki/Prikaz" title="Prikaz">Prikaz</a> (Military Appointment) headed by a <a href="/wiki/Okolnichy" title="Okolnichy">district official</a> from <a href="/wiki/Belgorod" title="Belgorod">Belgorod</a>. By 1657 the Kharkiv settlement had a fortress<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> with underground passageways.</p>
<p>In 1658 Ivan Ofrosimov was appointed as the new voivode, who worked on forcing locals to kiss the cross to show loyalty to the Moscow tsar.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The locals led by their <a href="/wiki/Otaman" class="mw-redirect" title="Otaman">otaman</a> Ivan Kryvoshlyk refused.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> However, with the election of the new otaman Tymish Lavrynov the community (hromada) sent a request to the tsar to establish a local Assumption market, signed by <a href="/wiki/Dean_(Christianity)" title="Dean (Christianity)">deans</a> of Kharkiv churches (the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Cathedral,_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Assumption Cathedral, Kharkiv">Assumption Cathedral</a> and parish churches of Annunciation and Trinity).<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> Relationships with the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Chuhuiv" title="Chuhuiv">Chuhuiv</a> sometimes were non-friendly and often their arguments were pacified by force.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> With the appointment of the third voivode Vasiliy Sukhotin was completely finished the construction of the city fort.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Kharkiv had become the centre of <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine" title="Sloboda Ukraine">Sloboda Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KvUah5e_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KvUah5e-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kharkiv_Fortress">Kharkiv Fortress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Kharkiv Fortress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

View of modern pedestrian bridge over Kharkiv River in Kharkiv</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kharkiv Fortress was erected around the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Cathedral,_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Assumption Cathedral, Kharkiv">Assumption Cathedral</a> and its castle was at <a href="/w/index.php?title=University_Hill,_Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="University Hill, Kharkiv (page does not exist)">University Hill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> It was between today's streets: vulytsia Kvitky-Osnovianenko, Constitution Square, Rose Luxemburg Square, Proletarian Square, and Cathedral Descent.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The fortress had 10 towers: Chuhuivska Tower, Moskovska Tower, Vestovska Tower, Tainytska Tower, Lopanska Corner Tower, Kharkivska Corner Tower and others.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The tallest was Vestovska, some 16 metres (52&#160;ft) tall,<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> while the shortest one was Tainytska which had a secret well 35 metres (115&#160;ft) deep.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The fortress had the Lopanski Gates.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1689 the fortress was expanded and included the Saint-Pokrov Cathedral and Monastery which was baptized<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> and became the center of local eparchy. Coincidentally in the same year in the vicinity of Kharkiv in <a href="/wiki/Kolomak" title="Kolomak">Kolomak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mazepa" title="Ivan Mazepa">Ivan Mazepa</a> was announced the <a href="/wiki/Hetmans_of_Ukrainian_Cossacks" title="Hetmans of Ukrainian Cossacks">Hetman of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> Next to the Saint-Pokrov Cathedral was located the Kharkiv Collegiate that was transferred from <a href="/wiki/Belgorod" title="Belgorod">Belgorod</a> to Kharkiv in 1726.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_Russian_Empire">In the Russian Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: In the Russian Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the course of the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Russia_in_1708%E2%80%931710" title="Administrative divisions of Russia in 1708–1710">administrative reform</a> carried out in 1708 by <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, the area was included into <a href="/wiki/Kiev_Governorate" title="Kiev Governorate">Kiev Governorate</a>. Kharkiv is specifically mentioned as one of the towns making a part of the governorate.<sup id="cite_ref-1708List_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1708List-16">[15]</a></sup> In 1727, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgorod_Governorate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Belgorod Governorate (page does not exist)">Belgorod Governorate</a> was split off, and Kharkiv moved to Belgoro Governorate. It was the center of a separate administrative unit, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv_Sloboda_Cossack_regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kharkiv Sloboda Cossack regiment (page does not exist)">Kharkiv Sloboda Cossack regiment</a>. The regiment at some point was detached from Belgorod Governorate, then attached to it again, until in 1765, <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Sloboda Ukraine Governorate">Sloboda Ukraine Governorate</a> was established with the seat in Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-voronezh_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voronezh-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kharkiv University">Kharkiv University</a> was established in 1805 in the Palace of <a href="/wiki/Governorate-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governorate-General">Governorate-General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aleksander_Mickiewicz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aleksander Mickiewicz (page does not exist)">Alexander Mikolajewicz Mickiewicz</a>, brother of <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz" title="Adam Mickiewicz">Adam Mickiewicz</a> was a professor of law in the university, another celebrity <a href="/wiki/Goethe" class="mw-redirect" title="Goethe">Goethe</a> searched for instructors for the school.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> In 1906 <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Franko" title="Ivan Franko">Ivan Franko</a> received a doctorate in Russian linguistics here.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The streets were first cobbled in the city centre in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> In 1844 the 90 metres (300&#160;ft) tall Alexander Bell Tower was built next to the first Assumption Cathedral, which on November 16, 1924 was transformed into a <a href="/wiki/Radio_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio tower">radio tower</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> A system of running water was established in 1870. The Cathedral Descent at one time carried the name of another local trader Vasyl Ivanovych Pashchenko-Tryapkin as Pashchenko Descent.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> Pashchenko even leased a space to the city council (duma) and was the owner of the city "Old Passage", the city's biggest trade center.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> After his death in 1894 Pashchenko donated all his possessions to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kharkiv became a major industrial centre and with it a centre of Ukrainian culture. In 1812, the first Ukrainian newspaper was published there.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> One of the first <a href="/wiki/Prosvita" title="Prosvita">Prosvitas</a> in Eastern Ukraine was also established in Kharkiv. A powerful nationally aware political movement was also established there and the concept of an Independent Ukraine was first declared there by the lawyer <a href="/wiki/Mykola_Mikhnovsky" title="Mykola Mikhnovsky">Mykola Mikhnovsky</a> in 1900.</p>
<p>Soon after the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>, in 1860–61 number of <a href="/wiki/Hromada_(secret_society)" title="Hromada (secret society)">hromada</a> societies sprung up across the Ukrainian cities including Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-hromada_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hromada-20">[19]</a></sup> Among the most prominent hromada members in Kharkiv was <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Potebnja" title="Alexander Potebnja">Oleksandr Potebnia</a>, a native of <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine" title="Sloboda Ukraine">Sloboda Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hromada_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hromada-20">[19]</a></sup> Beside the old hromada, in Kharkiv also existed several student hromadas members of which were future political leaders of Ukraine such as <a href="/wiki/Borys_Martos" title="Borys Martos">Borys Martos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmytro_Antonovych" title="Dmytro Antonovych">Dmytro Antonovych</a> and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-hromada_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hromada-20">[19]</a></sup> One of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Kharkiv">University of Kharkiv</a> graduates <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oleksandr_Kovalenko_(soldier)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oleksandr Kovalenko (soldier) (page does not exist)">Oleksandr Kovalenko</a> was one of initiators of the mutiny on <a href="/wiki/Russian_battleship_Potemkin" title="Russian battleship Potemkin">Russian battleship Potemkin</a> being the only officer who supported the in-rank sailors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_period">Soviet period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Soviet period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:(42)_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg/150px-%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg" width="150" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg/225px-%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg/300px-%2842%29_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:(42)_DERZHPROM_BUILDING_IN_CITY_OF_KHARKIV_STATE_OF_UKRAINE_PHOTOGRAPH_BY_VIKTOR_O_LEDENYOV_20160621.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of renovated <a href="/wiki/Derzhprom" title="Derzhprom">Derzhprom</a> building</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Piatykhatky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Piatykhatky.jpg/150px-Piatykhatky.jpg" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Piatykhatky.jpg/225px-Piatykhatky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Piatykhatky.jpg/300px-Piatykhatky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piatykhatky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial to the thousands of Ukrainian intellectuals murdered by the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> in 1937–38</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Tsentralna_Rada" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsentralna Rada">Tsentralna Rada</a> announced the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukrainian People's Republic</a> in November 1917 it envisioned the <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Sloboda Ukraine Governorate">Sloboda Ukraine Governorate</a> to be part of it.<sup id="cite_ref-KUW231114_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KUW231114-3">[2]</a></sup> In December 1917 Kharkiv became the first city in Ukraine occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet power">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Group_of_forces_in_battle_with_the_counterrevolution_in_the_South_of_Russia" title="Group of forces in battle with the counterrevolution in the South of Russia">troops</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Antonov-Ovseyenko" title="Vladimir Antonov-Ovseyenko">Vladimir Antonov-Ovseyenko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hdU_Katchanovski_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdU_Katchanovski-21">[20]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> in the Tsentralna Rada moved to Kharkiv shortly after to make it their stronghold and formed their own Rada on 13 December 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-hdU_Katchanovski_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdU_Katchanovski-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> By February 1918 Bolshevik forces had <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">captured much of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> In February 1918 Kharkiv became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Donetsk-Krivoy_Rog_Soviet_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Donetsk-Krivoy Rog Soviet Republic">Donetsk-Krivoy Rog Soviet Republic</a>; but this entity was disbanded six weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> In April 1918 the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">German army</a> occupied Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> And according to the February 1918 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk_(Ukraine%E2%80%93Central_Powers)" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk (Ukraine–Central Powers)">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> between the Ukrainian People's Republic and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> it became part of the Ukrainian People's Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Early January 1919 Bolshevik forces captured Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-KvUah5e_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KvUah5e-15">[14]</a></sup> Mid-June 1919 <a href="/wiki/Anton_Denikin" title="Anton Denikin">Anton Denikin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a> <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_Army" title="Volunteer Army">Volunteer Army</a> captured the city.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In December 1919 the Bolshevik <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> recaptured Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a> established Kharkiv as the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">capital</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (from 1919 to 1934) in opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukrainian People's Republic</a> with its capital of <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pamiatnyk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pamiatnyk.jpg/150px-Pamiatnyk.jpg" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pamiatnyk.jpg/225px-Pamiatnyk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pamiatnyk.jpg/300px-Pamiatnyk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="4050" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pamiatnyk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument to the <a href="/wiki/Persecuted_bandurists" title="Persecuted bandurists">persecuted kobzars</a> in Kharkiv</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to linguist <a href="/wiki/George_Shevelov" title="George Shevelov">George Shevelov</a>, in the early 1920s the share of <a href="/wiki/Secondary_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary schools">secondary schools</a> teaching in the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian language</a> was lower than the share of the <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Oblast" title="Kharkiv Oblast">Kharkiv Oblasts</a> ethnic <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainian</a> population,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> even though the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> had ordered that all schools in the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a> should be Ukrainian speaking (as part of its <a href="/wiki/Ukrainization" title="Ukrainization">Ukrainization</a> policy).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the country's capital, it underwent intense expansion with the construction of buildings to house the newly established Ukrainian Soviet government and administration. <a href="/wiki/Derzhprom" title="Derzhprom">Derzhprom</a> was the second tallest building in Europe and the tallest in the Soviet Union at the time with a height of 63 metres (207&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> In the 1920s, a 150 metres (490&#160;ft) wooden radio tower was built on top of the building. The Roentgen Institute was established in 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-Socialist_Health_Association_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Socialist_Health_Association-33">[32]</a></sup> During the interwar period the city saw the spread of architectural <a href="/wiki/Constructivism_(art)" title="Constructivism (art)">constructivism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> One of the best representatives of it was the already mentioned Derzhprom, the Building of the Red Army, the Ukrainian Polytechnic Institute of Distance Learning (UZPI), the City Council building, with its massive asymmetric tower, the central department store that was opened on the 15th Anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup> The same year on November 7, 1932 the building of Noblemen Assembly was transformed into the building of <a href="/wiki/Central_Executive_Committee_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Executive Committee of Ukraine">All-Ukrainian Central Executive Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1928, the SVU (<a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Freedom_of_Ukraine_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Union for the Freedom of Ukraine process">Union for the Freedom of Ukraine</a>) process was initiated and court sessions were staged in the Kharkiv Opera (now the Philharmonia) building. Hundreds of Ukrainian intellectuals were arrested and deported.</p>
<p>In the early 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a> famine drove many people off the land into the cities, and to Kharkiv in particular, in search of food. Many people died and were secretly buried in mass graves in the cemeteries surrounding the city.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg/150px-Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg/225px-Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg/300px-Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharkiv-Katyn2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial to the thousands of Polish officers executed by the NKVD in Kharkiv as part of the <a href="/wiki/Katyn_massacre" title="Katyn massacre">Katyn</a> massacre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1934&#160;hundreds of Ukrainian writers, intellectuals and cultural workers were arrested and executed in the attempt to eradicate all vestiges of Ukrainian nationalism in Art. The purges continued into 1938. Blind Ukrainian street musicians were also gathered in Kharkiv and murdered by the NKVD.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> In January 1934 the capital of the Ukrainian SSR was moved from Kharkiv to Kiev.<sup id="cite_ref-George_O._Liber_1992_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-George_O._Liber_1992-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>During April and May&#160;1940 about 3,900&#160;Polish prisoners of <a href="/wiki/Starobelsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Starobelsk">Starobelsk</a> camp were executed in the Kharkiv <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> building, later secretly buried on the grounds of an NKVD pansionat in <a href="/wiki/Piatykhatky,_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Piatykhatky, Kharkiv">Pyatykhatky</a> forest (part of the <a href="/wiki/Katyn_massacre" title="Katyn massacre">Katyn massacre</a>) on the outskirts of Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-Fischer_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer-37">[36]</a></sup> The site also contains the numerous bodies of Ukrainian cultural workers who were arrested and shot in the 1937–38 Stalinist purges.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_occupation">German occupation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: German occupation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG/150px-23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG/225px-23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG/300px-23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:23_August_Lane_Kharkov.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial to 23 August 1943, the end of German occupation during World War II</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Kharkiv was the site of several military engagements (see below). The city was captured and recaptured by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> on 24 October 1941;<sup id="cite_ref-kharkiv_at_war_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kharkiv_at_war-38">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> there was a disastrous <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> offensive that failed to capture the city in May 1942;<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> the city was successfully retaken by the Soviets on 16 February 1943, captured for a second time by the Germans on 15 March 1943 and then finally liberated on 23 August 1943. Seventy percent of the city was destroyed and tens of thousands of the inhabitants were killed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kharkiv, the third largest city in the Soviet Union, was the most populous city in the Soviet Union captured by the Germans, since in the years preceding World War II, <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> was by population the smaller of the two.</p>
<p>The significant Jewish population of Kharkiv (Kharkiv's Jewish community prided itself with the second largest synagogue in Europe) suffered greatly during the war. Between December 1941 and January 1942, an estimated 30,000 people<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (slightly more than half Jewish) were killed and buried in a mass grave by the Germans in a ravine outside of town named <a href="/wiki/Drobytsky_Yar" title="Drobytsky Yar">Drobytsky Yar</a>.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">World War II</a>, four battles took place for control of the city:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="First Battle of Kharkov">First Battle of Kharkov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Second Battle of Kharkov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Third Battle of Kharkov">Third Battle of Kharkov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fourth_Battle_of_Kharkov" class="mw-redirect" title="Fourth Battle of Kharkov">Fourth Battle of Kharkov</a> (<i>see also</i> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Polkovodets_Rumyantsev" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Polkovodets Rumyantsev">Operation Polkovodets Rumyantsev</a>)</li>
</ul>
<p>Before the occupation, Kharkiv's <a href="/wiki/Malyshev_Factory" title="Malyshev Factory">tank industries</a> were evacuated to the <a href="/wiki/Urals" class="mw-redirect" title="Urals">Urals</a> with all their equipment, and became the heart of <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>'s tank programs (particularly, producing the <a href="/wiki/T-34" title="T-34">T-34</a> tank earlier designed in Kharkiv). These enterprises returned to Kharkiv after the war, and continue to produce tanks.</p>
<p>Of the population of 700,000 that Kharkiv had before the start of World War II, 120,000 became <a href="/wiki/Ost-Arbeiter" class="mw-redirect" title="Ost-Arbeiter">Ost-Arbeiter</a> (<a href="/wiki/Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave">slave</a> worker) in Germany, 30,000 were executed and 80,000 starved to death during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-KvUah5e_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KvUah5e-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the post-World War II period many of the destroyed homes and factories were rebuilt. From the <a href="/wiki/Constructivism_(art)" title="Constructivism (art)">constructivism</a> the city was planned to be rebuilt in the style of <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Stalinist Classicism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-living_kharkiv_14-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-living_kharkiv-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>An airport was built in 1954. Following the war Kharkiv was the third largest scientific-industrial centre in the former USSR (after Moscow and <a href="/wiki/Leningrad" class="mw-redirect" title="Leningrad">Leningrad</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_independent_Ukraine">In independent Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: In independent Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IMG_2428_zerk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/IMG_2428_zerk.jpg/150px-IMG_2428_zerk.jpg" width="150" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/IMG_2428_zerk.jpg/225px-IMG_2428_zerk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/IMG_2428_zerk.jpg/300px-IMG_2428_zerk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="666" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IMG_2428_zerk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Zerkal%CA%B9naya_struya" title="Zerkalʹnaya struya">Mirror Stream</a> fountain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By its territorial expansion on September 6, 2012 the city increased its area from about 310 to 350 square kilometres (120 to 140&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>A well-known landmark of Kharkiv is the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Kharkiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom Square, Kharkiv">Freedom Square</a> (<i>Ploshcha Svobody</i> formerly known as <i>Dzerzhinsky Square</i>), which is the sixth largest city square in Europe, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_city_squares_by_size" title="List of city squares by size">12th largest square in the world</a>.</p>
<p>There is an underground <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Metro" title="Kharkiv Metro">rapid-transit system</a> (metro) with about 38.1&#160;km (24&#160;mi) of track and 29&#160;stations. The new "Victory" underground station (no. 30) was opened in Kharkiv on 19 August 2016. All the underground stations have very special distinctive architectures.</p>
<p>Kharkiv was a host city for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>, and hosted three group soccer matches at the reconstructed <a href="/wiki/Metalist_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Metalist Stadium">Metalist Stadium</a>.</p>
<p>A large number of the Orthodox cathedrals were built in Kharkiv in the 1990s and 2000s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>For example, the Peace Bringing Wives Orthodox cathedral, the St. Vladimir Orthodox cathedral, St. Tamara Orthodox cathedral, etc.</p>
<p>In 2007, the Vietnamese minority in Kharkiv built the largest Buddhist temple in Europe on a 1 hectare plot with a monument to <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gor'ky park was fully renovated in Kharkiv in the 2000s, having a big number of modern attractions, a lake with lilies and the sport facilities to play tennis, football, beach volleyball, and basketball.</p>
<p>The Feldman park was created in Kharkiv in recent years, containing a big collection of animals, horses, etc.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharkiv,_Ukraine,_city_and_vicinities,_LandSat-5_satellite_image,_near_natural_colors,_2011-06-18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg/150px-Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg" width="150" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg/225px-Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg/300px-Kharkiv%2C_Ukraine%2C_city_and_vicinities%2C_LandSat-5_satellite_image%2C_near_natural_colors%2C_2011-06-18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2461" data-file-height="2577" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kharkiv,_Ukraine,_city_and_vicinities,_LandSat-5_satellite_image,_near_natural_colors,_2011-06-18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kharkiv and vicinities, LandSat-5 satellite image, near natural colors, 2011-06-18</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kharkiv is located at the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_River" title="Kharkiv River">Kharkiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lopan_River" title="Lopan River">Lopan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Udy_River" title="Udy River">Udy</a> rivers, where they flow into the <a href="/wiki/Seversky_Donets" class="mw-redirect" title="Seversky Donets">Seversky Donets</a> watershed in the North-Eastern region of Ukraine.</p>
<p>Historically, Kharkiv lies in the <a href="/wiki/Sloboda_Ukraine" title="Sloboda Ukraine">Sloboda Ukraine</a> region (<i>Slobozhanshchyna</i> also known as <i>Slobidshchyna</i>) in Ukraine, in which it is considered as a main city.</p>
<p>The approximate dimensions of City of Kharkiv are: from the North to the South - 24.3&#160;km; from the West to the East — 25.2&#160;km.</p>
<p>Based on Kharkiv's topography, the city can be conditionally divided on the four lower districts and the four higher districts.</p>
<p>The highest point over the sea level in Pyatikhatky in Kharkiv is 202m, the lowest point over the sea level in Novoselivka in Kharkiv is 94m.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kharkiv lies in the large valley of rivers of <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_River" title="Kharkiv River">Kharkiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lopan_River" title="Lopan River">Lopan'</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udy_River" title="Udy River">Udy</a>, and Nemyshlya. This valley lies from the North West to the South East between the Mid Russian highland and Donetsk lowland. All the rivers interconnect in Kharkiv and flow into the river of <a href="/wiki/Seversky_Donets" class="mw-redirect" title="Seversky Donets">Northern Donets</a>. A special system of the concrete and metal dams was designed and built by engineers to regulate the water level in the rivers in Kharkiv.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kharkiv has a large number of the green city parks with the long history of more than 100 years with very old oak trees and many flowers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kharkiv's climate is <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfb</i>) with cold and snowy winters as well as the dry and hot summers.</p>
<p>Kharkiv has rather sunny warm summers which, however, are relatively mild compared to temperatures in South European regions, due to the region's lower elevation, proximity to the Black Sea, and the city's <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>. In other words, Kharkiv experiences the warm summers, interrupted by only occasional, brief intervals of stormy rain conditions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kharkiv has relatively long and cold winters.</p>
<p>The average rainfall totals 513&#160;mm (20&#160;in) per year, with the most in June and July.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status_and_local_government">Legal status and local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Legal status and local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Mayor of Kharkiv and the City Council govern all the business and administrative affairs in the City of Kharkiv.</p>
<p>The Mayor of Kharkiv has the executive powers; the City Council has the administrative powers as far as the government issues is concerned.</p>
<p>The Mayor of Kharkiv is elected by the direct public election in Kharkiv every four years.</p>
<p>The City Council is composed of elected representatives, who approve or reject the initiatives on the budget allocation, tasks priorities and other issues in Kharkiv. The representatives to the City Council are elected every four years.</p>
<p>The mayor and city council hold their regular meetings in the City Hall in Kharkiv.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine#Kharkiv_Oblast" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine §&#160;Kharkiv Oblast</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine</a> affected Kharkiv but to a lesser extent than in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Donbass" title="Donbass">Donbass</a>, where tensions would lead to <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">armed conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ukraine_crisis_timeline_BBC_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine_crisis_timeline_BBC-46">[45]</a></sup> On 2 March 2014, a Russian "tourist" from Moscow replaced the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian flag">Ukrainian flag</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Russian_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian flag">Russian flag</a> on the Kharkiv regional state administration building.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Five days later, pro-Russian protestors occupied the building and unilaterally declared independence from Ukraine as the "Kharkov People's Republic".<sup id="cite_ref-Focus_Information_Agency_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Focus_Information_Agency-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LiveLeak.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiveLeak.com-49">[48]</a></sup> The next day, the building was retaken by Ukrainian special forces.<sup id="cite_ref-KRR2_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KRR2-50">[49]</a></sup> Doubts arose about the local origin of the protestors after they initially stormed an opera and ballet theatre believing it was the city hall.<sup id="cite_ref-MT140408_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MT140408-51">[50]</a></sup> On 13 April, some pro-Russian protesters again made it inside the Kharkiv regional state administration building.<sup id="cite_ref-kharkivinfiltrate_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kharkivinfiltrate-52">[51]</a></sup> Later on 13 April the building returned permanently to full Ukrainian control.<sup id="cite_ref-Focus_Information_Agency_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Focus_Information_Agency-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LiveLeak.com_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiveLeak.com-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KRR2_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KRR2-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kharkivinfiltrate_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kharkivinfiltrate-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kernessep_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kernessep-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DWBaluta_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWBaluta-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unian.net_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unian.net-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OSCEmonitor_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCEmonitor-56">[55]</a></sup> Violent clashes resulted in the severe beating of at least 50 pro-Ukrainian protesters in attacks by pro-Russian protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-kharkivinfiltrate_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kharkivinfiltrate-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unian.net_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unian.net-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kharkiv returned to relative calm by 30 April.<sup id="cite_ref-OSCEmonitor30_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCEmonitor30-57">[56]</a></sup> Relatively peaceful demonstrations continued to be held, with "pro-Russian" rallies gradually diminishing and "pro-Ukrainian unity" demonstrations growing in numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-OSCE624_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCE624-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OSCE257_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCE257-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Status_quo_17814_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Status_quo_17814-60">[59]</a></sup> On 28 September, activists dismantled Ukraine's largest monument to Lenin at a pro-Ukrainian rally in the central square.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Polls conducted from September to December 2014 found little support in Kharkiv for joining Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Navalny140923_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Navalny140923-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DT150103_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT150103-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>From early November until mid-December, Kharkiv was struck by seven non-lethal bomb blasts. Targets of these attacks included a rock pub known for raising money for Ukrainian forces, a hospital for Ukrainian forces, a military recruiting centre, and a <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_Ukraine" title="National Guard of Ukraine">National Guard</a> base.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">SBU</a> investigator <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vasyliy_Vovk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vasyliy Vovk (page does not exist)">Vasyliy Vovk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Intelligence_Service_(Russia)" title="Foreign Intelligence Service (Russia)">Russian covert forces</a> were behind the attacks, and had intended to destabilize the otherwise calm city of Kharkiv.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 January 2015 five men wearing <a href="/wiki/Balaclava_(clothing)" title="Balaclava (clothing)">balaclavas</a> broke into an office of (the volunteer group aiding refugees from <a href="/wiki/Donbass" title="Donbass">Donbass</a>) <i>Station Kharkiv</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-biSK8115_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biSK8115-66">[65]</a></sup> Simultaneously with physical threats the men demanded to hear the political position of <i>Station Kharkiv</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-biSK8115_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biSK8115-66">[65]</a></sup> After being given an answer the men apologized and left.<sup id="cite_ref-biSK8115_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biSK8115-66">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Sunday 22 February 2015, there was a terrorist bomb attack on a march to commemorate people who died in the Euromaidan protests in 2014. The bomb killed two, and wounded nine. The authorities have launched an anti-terrorist operation.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> The terrorists claim that it was a false flag attack.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Kharkiv experienced more non-lethal small bombings since 22 February 2015 targeting army fuel tanks, an unoccupied passenger train and a <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian flag">Ukrainian flag</a> in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 September 2015, 200 people in balaclavas and camouflage picketed the house of former governor <a href="/wiki/Mykhailo_Dobkin" title="Mykhailo Dobkin">Mykhailo Dobkin</a>, and then went to Kharkiv town hall, where they tried to force their way through the police cordon. At least one tear gas grenade was used. The rioters asked the mayor, <a href="/wiki/Hennadiy_Kernes" title="Hennadiy Kernes">Hennadiy Kernes</a>, to come out.<sup id="cite_ref-Unian23Sep151410_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unian23Sep151410-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While Kharkiv is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">administrative centre</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Oblast" title="Kharkiv Oblast">Kharkiv Oblast</a> (<a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Ukraine" title="Administrative divisions of Ukraine">province</a>), the city affairs are managed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv_City_Municipality&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kharkiv City Municipality (page does not exist)">Kharkiv Municipality</a>. Kharkiv is a <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Ukraine" title="Administrative divisions of Ukraine">city of oblast subordinance</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg/150px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg.png" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg/225px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg/300px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Administrative divisions of Kharkiv</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The territory of Kharkiv is divided into 9 administrative <a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Districts" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts">districts</a>), till February 2016 they were named for people, places, events, and organizations associated with early years of the Soviet Union but many were renamed in February 2016 to comply with <a href="/wiki/Decommunization_in_Ukraine" title="Decommunization in Ukraine">decommunization laws</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nmcrinK_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmcrinK-4">[3]</a></sup> Also, owing to this law, over 200 streets have been renamed in Kharkiv since 20 November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The raions are named:<sup id="cite_ref-nmcrinK_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmcrinK-4">[3]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>Kholodnohirskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Холодногірський район</span>, <i>Cold Mountain</i>; namesake: the historic name of the neighbourhood<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup>) (formerly Leninskyi; namesake: <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>)</li>
<li>Shevchenkivskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Шевченківський район</span>); namesake: <a href="/wiki/Taras_Shevchenko" title="Taras Shevchenko">Taras Shevchenko</a> (formerly Dzerzhynskyi; namesake <a href="/wiki/Felix_Dzerzhinsky" title="Felix Dzerzhinsky">Felix Dzerzhinsky</a>)</li>
<li>Kyivskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Київський район</span>); namesake: <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a></li>
<li>Moskovskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Московський район</span>); namesake: <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a></li>
<li>Nemyshlianskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Немишлянський район</span>);</li>
<li>Industrialnyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Індустріальний район</span>) (formerly Ordzhonikidzevskyi; namesake: <a href="/wiki/Sergo_Ordzhonikidze" title="Sergo Ordzhonikidze">Sergo Ordzhonikidze</a>)</li>
<li>Slobidskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Слобідський район</span>);</li>
<li>Osnovianskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Основ'янський район</span>);</li>
<li>Novobavarskyi (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Новобаварський район</span>)</li>
</ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kharkiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:auto">Year</th>

<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Census_(1989)" title="Soviet Census (1989)">1989 Soviet Union Census</a>, the population of the city was 1,593,970. In 1991, the population decreased to 1,510,200, including 1,494,200 permanent city residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_Kharkiv_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_Kharkiv-85">[84]</a></sup> Kharkiv is the second-largest city in Ukraine after the capital, <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ukrcensus1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukrcensus1-86">[85]</a></sup> The first independent all-Ukrainian population census was conducted in December 2001, and the next all-Ukrainian population census is decreed to be conduced in 2020. As of 2001, the population of the Kharkiv region is as follows: 78.5% living in urban areas, and 21.5% living in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
